  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5f89f90b-0653-4a74-a1e4-0d6a907de6f5'
      });

<div id="review_1317838129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1317838129" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1317838129?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061375378" href="/book/show/6562891-horizon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1317838129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17794830652042895051">Eight or more years ago, I bought and read the first book in this series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61898.Beguilement__The_Sharing_Knife___1_' title='Beguilement (The Sharing Knife, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beguilement</a>, but never felt particularly motivated to finish the 4-book series until a few weeks ago. It occurred to me that before I let my (expensive non-resident) library card lapse for the next few months, I should grab this series off the library's shelves and plow or skim through it, as the spirit moved me.<br/><br/>The second book was a skimmer for me (I didn't rate or review it because of the amount I skipped over), but the </span>
  <span id="freeText17794830652042895051" style="display:none">Eight or more years ago, I bought and read the first book in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61898.Beguilement__The_Sharing_Knife___1_" title="Beguilement (The Sharing Knife, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Beguilement</a>, but never felt particularly motivated to finish the 4-book series until a few weeks ago. It occurred to me that before I let my (expensive non-resident) library card lapse for the next few months, I should grab this series off the library's shelves and plow or skim through it, as the spirit moved me.<br><br>The second book was a skimmer for me (I didn't rate or review it because of the amount I skipped over), but the third was good enough that I actually read the whole thing with a fair amount of interest, especially the last part, which really ramped up the intensity. The excitement kind of ramps down again at the start of this fourth and final volume in the series, but I found myself unexpectedly taken with the telling of Dag and Fawn's stay with a camp of Lakewalkers, where Dag can learn from others how to use and control his abilities as a maker and healer. The magical aspects of this were fascinating. <br><br>Dag and Fawn are still battling the prejudices that Dag's people, the Lakewalkers, have against Fawn's, the farmers, and vice versa. Specifically, Lakewalkers don't like Dag practicing his healing abilities on farmers. But when a young farmer boy gets lockjaw from stepping on a nail, what's a self-respecting healer to do? And one thing leads to another, and of course Dag and Fawn and their friends aren't finished dealing with the deadly malices that blight their lands. And one malice is of a sort that no one's ever seen before:<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435625266i/15366034._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>This book turned out to be a lot more interesting and exciting than I was expecting. I wasn't sure if Bujold could find a way to wrap up the series that would be both believable and satisfying to me, but she did it. It's definitely my favorite book of this western frontier fantasy series.<br><br>Bujold is a very creative and talented author who writes believable characters. I'm not sure if I'd recommend plowing through the entire series unless (a) a frontier era fantasy sounds interesting, and (b) you don't mind a large side helping of May/December romance. But I can tell you that, at least in my opinion, if you do, you won't be disappointed by the ending of the series.<br><br>4.5 stars.<br><br>Art credit: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pre09.deviantart.net/b043/th/pre/i/2012/036/5/0/dc_antiquity___man_bat_by_dustsplat-d4osulz.jpg">http://pre09.deviantart.net/b043/th/p...</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17794830652042895051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_46516546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46516546" />
    <a title="Kate Coombs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/235385-kate-coombs"><img alt="Kate Coombs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231619578p2/235385.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46516546?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Coombs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Coombs" href="/user/show/235385-kate-coombs">Kate Coombs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46516546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11390895686242858825">I figured out a long time ago that Lois McMaster Bujold is one of THOSE authors--basically, if she writes a book, it's good. Period. And the Sharing Knife books are no exception. McMaster Bujold's worlds feel real, and her characters matter. This series is a little slower paced than some of her science fiction, but they're still very rewarding reading.<br/><br/>Horizon is the fourth book in the Sharing Knife series, in which a farmer girl and a one-armed Lakewalker man meet while fighting a terrible monst</span>
  <span id="freeText11390895686242858825" style="display:none">I figured out a long time ago that Lois McMaster Bujold is one of THOSE authors--basically, if she writes a book, it's good. Period. And the Sharing Knife books are no exception. McMaster Bujold's worlds feel real, and her characters matter. This series is a little slower paced than some of her science fiction, but they're still very rewarding reading.<br /><br />Horizon is the fourth book in the Sharing Knife series, in which a farmer girl and a one-armed Lakewalker man meet while fighting a terrible monster and end up marrying. However, in this land, farmers and Lakewalkers generally avoid each other. The Lakewalkers despise the farmers for having no magic (groundsense); the farmers fear the Lakewalkers for their magic and because the Lakewalkers make knives out of their dead kins' bones. What the farmers do not understand is that the sharing knives--imbued with the souls of the dying--are the only weapon capable of destroying the terrible malices (which are kind of like the Star Trek's Borg, only more organic--see my review of Jim Butcher's Alera books!). Lakewalkers hunt malices, and if they didn't, the land would soon be overrun and destroyed.<br /><br />As Dag and Fawn deal with both malices and malicious humans, they see clearly what no one else has realized: that the rift between farmers and Lakewalkers inadvertently benefits the malices. The seemingly mismatched couple sets out to change prejudices and find solutions, ultimately a greater challenge than slaying a malice.<br /><br />In the crowded sci-fi/fantasy realm, not many authors stand out, but Lois McMaster Bujold is so good she scarcely has any competition. Of course, if you're going to read about Dag and Fawn, you should start with Book One and travel the author's land clear to the Horizon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11390895686242858825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77589851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17159676324796331117">In which this four-book romance fantasy wanders – by which I mean plot? What plot? – to a close – by which I mean babies for all!<br/><br/>Yikes. A friend called this the "never-ending beige adventure," which made me laugh. More than the book did.<br/><br/>I'm feeling kind of cranky about this book. It's intellectually boring, with a thematic conversation (communication, clashing and changing paradigms, etc.) little deeper than your average morality play. I could forgive intellectual boredom for emotional interest </span>
  <span id="freeText17159676324796331117" style="display:none">In which this four-book romance fantasy wanders – by which I mean plot? What plot? – to a close – by which I mean babies for all!<br /><br />Yikes. A friend called this the "never-ending beige adventure," which made me laugh. More than the book did.<br /><br />I'm feeling kind of cranky about this book. It's intellectually boring, with a thematic conversation (communication, clashing and changing paradigms, etc.) little deeper than your average morality play. I could forgive intellectual boredom for emotional interest – God knows I've done <i>that</i> before. But my emotional needle didn't so much as quiver throughout. I will say that the book is at least prettily, if . . . rustically written. And I don't usually get cranky over boring, because boring for me is a great romance for someone else (though, I've never met anyone who was actually really moved by this particular series . . . Bueller?).<br /><br />No, the real problem is the explicit and implicit helping of babymaking propaganda. Did you guys <i>know</i> that the purpose of marriage is babies? Didya didya didya? The sheer amount of moral imperative this series piles on reproduction – though, okay, not always heteronormatively – is staggering because half of it is delivered with this 'duh' of universal unarguable truth, which, um, no, and the other half feels entirely unconscious and kind of uncomfortable as a glimpse of author id to me. The older I get, the more toxic that becomes. Yeurgh.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17159676324796331117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_420037084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420037084" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37948-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1276625239p2/37948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420037084?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/37948-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37948-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37948-julia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37948-julia?shelf=women-in-spec-fic">women-in-spec-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420037084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8714294868342472211">I'm not sure why I kept reading this series, since I didn't like it very much. A different series by this author (the Miles Vorkosigan series) is a funny, clever space opera with interesting characters and plots, and I had tremendous fun tearing through the whole series in a month. This series was a fantasy romance, emphasis on the romance, which would be fine if the characters were interesting. They're not, particularly. The heroine is a Mary Sue; spunky, loyal, clever, compassionate, and perfe</span>
  <span id="freeText8714294868342472211" style="display:none">I'm not sure why I kept reading this series, since I didn't like it very much. A different series by this author (the Miles Vorkosigan series) is a funny, clever space opera with interesting characters and plots, and I had tremendous fun tearing through the whole series in a month. This series was a fantasy romance, emphasis on the romance, which would be fine if the characters were interesting. They're not, particularly. The heroine is a Mary Sue; spunky, loyal, clever, compassionate, and perfect, with a little totally unfounded insecurity to keep her from being arrogant. She had premarital sex the one time, but that's not a flaw, and nobody in-world who isn't a villain thinks it is either. <br /><br />The hero isn't much better, being one of those Alpha Jacks of All Trades. Of all the characters we meet, his magic range is the biggest. His malice (series' main villain) kill tally is the highest. Whenever there's a fight, he's in charge. During the course of the series it's discovered he's also a healing prodigy, and a maker (mage), the two highest-status positions in his society. He's missing a hand, but it doesn't slow him down! He has a variety of stump attachments suitable for any need, including a bow, and he's a great shot! Gag me with a spoon. Occasionally he's glum. That's about it.<br /><br />They fall in love in two days, and never have a serious fight. They spend a lot of time being understanding and patient, which I'm sure is a nice way to behave, but we never see them struggle to arrive at that understanding or lose that patience, which makes it seem contrived. Why is their relationship so strong? Well, because they're just such marvelous people! But they're lousy characters because they're boring to read about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8714294868342472211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2631727867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14874868932570082485">Mini-Review: <br/><br/>YAY for narration by Bernadette Dunne! I've heard her before but now I will keep an eye out for her name on audiobooks. I really enjoyed her style of narration for this series. <br/><br/>I liked it. It wasn't quite what I was expecting but it worked. I should have realized by the second book that the series would be more about the journey of making changes rather than finding a particular answer. The focus moved from being about Dag and Fawn to showing the reader the world in which they lived</span>
  <span id="freeText14874868932570082485" style="display:none">Mini-Review: <br /><br />YAY for narration by Bernadette Dunne! I've heard her before but now I will keep an eye out for her name on audiobooks. I really enjoyed her style of narration for this series. <br /><br />I liked it. It wasn't quite what I was expecting but it worked. I should have realized by the second book that the series would be more about the journey of making changes rather than finding a particular answer. The focus moved from being about Dag and Fawn to showing the reader the world in which they lived and how much harm can happen due to ignorance and fear of the unknown. It means something when the series is over and you're left wondering what happened to all of the characters that you've gotten to know. I definitely feel that wistful note here at the end. <br /><br />Horizon was an adventure story that teaches about being open to trying new things, working with failure and noting that change may be full of prickly pangs but also goodness. <br /><br />It was a nice jaunt into a different world and full of great characters that I enjoyed getting to know. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14874868932570082485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_139745675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139745675" />
    <a title="Scott Marlowe (Out of this World Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1365845-scott-marlowe-out-of-this-world-reviews"><img alt="Scott Marlowe (Out of this World Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581359944p2/1365845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139745675?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Marlowe (Out of this World Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Marlowe (Out of this World Reviews)" href="/user/show/1365845-scott-marlowe-out-of-this-world-reviews">Scott Marlowe (Out of this World Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139745675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7793695145260918812">Rating<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507206351i/24091002.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Review<br/><br/>*** This review originally appeared on <a href='http://outofthisworldreviews.com/post/Horizon-by-Lois-McMaster-Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Out of this World Reviews</a>. ***<br/><br/>Horizon is the fourth and final book of Bujold's Sharing Knife series. In it, we find our heroes, Dag and Fawn Bluefield, returning north with the intention of settling a place of their own. Dag, already a veteran Lakewalker patroller, has become more than that now: medicine-maker, groundsetter, husband, father/brother figure, and all-around leader to a small conclave of Lakewalkers and farmers. Dag wants for simple</span>
  <span id="freeText7793695145260918812" style="display:none">Rating<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507206351i/24091002.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Review<br><br>*** This review originally appeared on <a href="http://outofthisworldreviews.com/post/Horizon-by-Lois-McMaster-Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Out of this World Reviews</a>. ***<br><br>Horizon is the fourth and final book of Bujold's Sharing Knife series. In it, we find our heroes, Dag and Fawn Bluefield, returning north with the intention of settling a place of their own. Dag, already a veteran Lakewalker patroller, has become more than that now: medicine-maker, groundsetter, husband, father/brother figure, and all-around leader to a small conclave of Lakewalkers and farmers. Dag wants for simple things, but his life is anything but simple. As he and Fawn and a myriad of others travel north, they come face-to-face with Dag's worst nightmare: a malice that has grown unchecked and become very powerful as a result.<br><br>The Sharing Knife is, by it's very definition, about sacrifice. Dag sacrifices his usual way of life as a Lakewalker. Fawn sacrifices the stability of the life of a farmer to be with him. Others cross paths with Lakewalkers and farmers alike throughout the series and oftentimes come away missing something. A sharing knife itself is a medium of sacrifice, for it is imbued with the 'death' of a Lakewalker individual, and is the only weapon that can slay a malice.<br><br>Horizon is very much a continuation (and conclusion) of the series. The story itself comes full circle in more ways than one as Dag and Fawn return north and, in inadvertent fashion, complete the quest most dear to Dag's heart: to seal the rift between farmer and Lakewalker and unite them against the common threat of malice. Perhaps the best thing about Horizon is the way in which this happens. I won't give anything away, but suffice to say Dag spends much of the first three books planting seeds which only spring forth in this final volume.<br><br>I've said this before, but it bears mentioning again: the four books read as one. The style, the flow of the various plotlines; one can easily imagine Bujold having written the series in one long, continuous sitting. The writing is consistently excellent, with characters true to form and dialog spot on. This is not an action-packed thriller, yet Bujold has an excellent sense of moving the story along. I never felt like she was spinning me in circles or going down a path that had no relevance to the overall story. It's just great storytelling.<br><br>I'm giving Horizon and the overall Sharing Knife series 5 out of 5 rockets. It really is an enjoyable read, with interesting characters, hints of suspense in all the right places, and a world that is believable and engaging. The 'magic system' is fresh and original, and not overdone in any sense. I'd recommend picking up a copy and giving it a read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7793695145260918812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45921226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45921226" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1282558-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214790635p2/1282558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45921226?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/1282558-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1282558-rebecca?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1282558-rebecca?shelf=non-earth">non-earth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1282558-rebecca?shelf=relationship-driven">relationship-driven</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45921226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17244280179854964845">So, I will endeavor to review the final book in a series without spoiling the other three.<br/><br/>Frankly, I'd hold up The Sharing Knife series as how to do a multi-book romance without plunging into unbelievable melodrama. The 'will they or won't they' is settled in the first book, leaving books 2-4 as a story of a young couple with a 'forbidden' relationship trying to carve a place in the world. Book 4 opens with Dag and Fawn in the south, where the problem of Lakewalkers and farmers is shown in high </span>
  <span id="freeText17244280179854964845" style="display:none">So, I will endeavor to review the final book in a series without spoiling the other three.<br /><br />Frankly, I'd hold up The Sharing Knife series as how to do a multi-book romance without plunging into unbelievable melodrama. The 'will they or won't they' is settled in the first book, leaving books 2-4 as a story of a young couple with a 'forbidden' relationship trying to carve a place in the world. Book 4 opens with Dag and Fawn in the south, where the problem of Lakewalkers and farmers is shown in high relief. The south hasn't had a malice attack in living memory, so Lakewalkers are forced to interact somewhat, but even then they don't have a solution that satisfies Dag. Dag is able to find a teacher for what he wants to do, though, and then strikes up north to return to the part of the country he grew up.<br /><br />I continue to like how things are set up. Fawn continues to be 'the smart one' in the relationship, something that Bujold never says but does a wonderful job of showing. A lot of times in 'normal'/'paranormal' relationship fiction I get the sense that the normal person is just a kind of placeholder, and Fawn is nothing like that. <br /><br />The book also does a good job of showing Dag-as-mage, in that some of what he does is reinvented because he didn't have access to a teacher, and some of what he does is innovative. I also like the interaction between him and his teacher, Arkady. <br /><br />The one problem I had with this book is that Bujold introduces a cast of characters for the trip north -- a group of settlers that Dag offers to help guide, another wagon that they help in the mountains, and a Lakewalker patrol led by Dag's niece. A lot happens with those -- one set of siblings are half-Lakewalker and the sister has both a decent amount of groundsense and a bad case of Caught-Between-Two-Worlds, both of which the party addresses. There's also a romance between Dag's niece and his teacher. A lot of these don't get as much time as I'd like, and some of the characters (the male settlers, for instance), blur together. It's possible I'll resolve this on a reread, but it was disenheartening in a series so good about character relationships.<br /><br />Overall, I do recommend this series as one of my favorite fantasies and romance-oriented fiction. I'd recommend the series to anyone who wants to see 'forbidden romance' done right, without either character abandoning his or her home culture but instead trying to forge a new path. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17244280179854964845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47952864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47952864" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/180908-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184048097p2/180908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47952864?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/180908-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180908-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer47952864&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47952864" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7341516491058843164">I was disappointed with this book, but possibly it's because I have this reaction to a lot of fantasy, that it's not made real enough to satisfy me. I had looked forward to understanding more of the whys of this world and its social setup. I want to know what malices are, and how they're related to Lakewalkers, and how they're both related to farmers, how it all came about on a planet which if it isn't Earth definitely has an uncanny resemblance to it in its fauna, flora, and even technology, di</span>
  <span id="freeText7341516491058843164" style="display:none">I was disappointed with this book, but possibly it's because I have this reaction to a lot of fantasy, that it's not made real enough to satisfy me. I had looked forward to understanding more of the whys of this world and its social setup. I want to know what malices are, and how they're related to Lakewalkers, and how they're both related to farmers, how it all came about on a planet which if it isn't Earth definitely has an uncanny resemblance to it in its fauna, flora, and even technology, diseases, tools, etc. Maybe I just don't get the assumptions of this genre or something. The story was fine. It came to a nice resolution. But the world was left completely unexplained, and that bugged me. I had thought it would all make a lot more sense in the end, I guess. <br /><br />Fantasy I like: I absolutely love Tolkien. I love Ursula K. LeGuin's Earthsea series. I love Octavia Butler's fantasy stuff, like that Vampire novel Fledgling, or the slavery one Kindred. It's fantasy but it makes sense. <br /><br />Fantasy I enjoyed but thought was mediocre: All the dragonriders of Pern stuff by Anne McCaffery, the Liveship Traders series by Robin Hobb, this series.<br /><br />Fantasy I've thought was really poor: Sherri Tepper, Animal Farm, any of those dystopia type warnings that are didactic in nature. In fact, I loathe didacticism in books that label themselves as stories. <br /><br />I enjoy Bujold's Vorkosigan books, though they're pretty lightweight for the most part, so I thought I would like this too. I can't say it wasn't entertaining for the most part, but I found it ultimately unsatisfying.<br /><br />An update because I reread this series recently, though I'm not sure why. I really enjoyed the relationship between Dag and Fawn this time through, and the way they treated each other. I liked how Dag took on and fostered these very annoying (in some cases) young people and helped them grow up well. I thought the building up of the group over time was really good, really meaty and true. I loved how real was the way their families treated them to start with, and how they built themselves a new family together that had a lot more respect and joy in it. So I added one star for that reason. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7341516491058843164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_175210414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="bananananas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2367192-bananananas"><img alt="bananananas" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175210414?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bananananas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bananananas" href="/user/show/2367192-bananananas">bananananas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2367192-bananananas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175210414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16216260545117713459">This series could have been so much better if it was less about the romance and more about...everything else. <br/><br/>The malices/mud-men/mages and all the back story with the Lakewalkers and their magic and whatnot was really compelling. The world was really interesting, and a lot was made of how dangerous the north is but we never get anything except for a vague reference to the character Dag's time spent up there. The whole story with how the Lakewalkers essentially need two deaths to be shaped into </span>
  <span id="freeText16216260545117713459" style="display:none">This series could have been so much better if it was less about the romance and more about...everything else. <br /><br />The malices/mud-men/mages and all the back story with the Lakewalkers and their magic and whatnot was really compelling. The world was really interesting, and a lot was made of how dangerous the north is but we never get anything except for a vague reference to the character Dag's time spent up there. The whole story with how the Lakewalkers essentially need two deaths to be shaped into a knife, and that knife to be used to teach a malice how to die was really interesting. There was so much potential story here...<br /><br />Too bad we instead only get to see how to destroy a pretty great character: when Dag gets mixed up with a farmgirl who has absolutely no personality. All I learned about Fawn was that she was curious (well, enough to get herself pregnant, which is how we meet her running away from home), tottered a lot (which puts me in mind of a toddler, and then makes me think of the age difference between her and Dag -- 37 years!), and tossed her head all the time like a self-involved preteen. There's absolutely no character growth for her. And her brother, who we're supposed to basically hate right from the start, becomes a more compelling character as the story drags along.<br /><br />If this series had been about the war between Lakewalkers and malices, with Dag and some of the other characters figuring out along the way that farmers need to be in on it too, this story would have been fantastic, especially in the hands of such a proven talent as Ms Bujold. If the romance had been a side-story it would have been interesting. Heck, if the female character had been less of a Mary Sue and more of an actual person, this story would have been fantastic! But it's not.<br /><br />And 3 stars because I read all four volumes, and why would I stick around just to give the whole thing a bad rating? </span>
  <a data-text-id="16216260545117713459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16014821925025850498">1st read: This book is wonderful and with a very satisfying ending too! I have so much enjoyed the "Sharing Knife" world--it is such an interesting fantasy 'take' on a alternate frontier America.<br/><br/>I especially enjoy how Lois McMaster Bujold portrays a strong marriage partnership with love, respect, and caring between two strong and multi-dimensional characters.   <span id="freeText16014821925025850498" style="display:none">1st read: This book is wonderful and with a very satisfying ending too! I have so much enjoyed the "Sharing Knife" world--it is such an interesting fantasy 'take' on a alternate frontier America.<br /><br />I especially enjoy how Lois McMaster Bujold portrays a strong marriage partnership with love, respect, and caring between two strong and multi-dimensional characters. One partner's weaknesses are counteracted by the other partner's strengths and vice versa. So that the couple is stronger together than apart--this is what true romance is to me. Their relationship "rings true" based on my life experience. I find this rare in many novels that I read, so I celebrate it when I come across it. <br /><br />This type of strong marriage and equal partnership shows up in LMB's other books, also in Diana Gabaldon's Outlander series, with Commander Vimes &amp; Lady Sybil in Terry Pratchett's Diskworld series and to some degree in J. Suzanne Frank's books. If you can think of any others, please feel free to recommend them to me.<br /><br />2nd read 10/2/11<br />3rd read 3/7/13</span>

<div id="review_498730711" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/498730711" />
    <a title="QuincyK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7130751-quincyk"><img alt="QuincyK" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/498730711?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="QuincyK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="QuincyK" href="/user/show/7130751-quincyk">QuincyK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer498730711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12014166892405289115">Basically, I'll review all four books of the Sharing Knife series in this review.<br/><br/>I wanted to read some of Bujold's fantasy after reading her fantastic Vorkosigan series. Unfortunately I started with the Sharing Knife series. <br/><br/>Coming from the Vorkosigan saga's excellent expression of complex characters and clearly delineated political systems, this series was a disappointment. <br/><br/>It has her usual themes from the Vorkosigan series: culture clash, younger woman/older man relationship, women's roles in </span>
  <span id="freeText12014166892405289115" style="display:none">Basically, I'll review all four books of the Sharing Knife series in this review.<br /><br />I wanted to read some of Bujold's fantasy after reading her fantastic Vorkosigan series. Unfortunately I started with the Sharing Knife series. <br /><br />Coming from the Vorkosigan saga's excellent expression of complex characters and clearly delineated political systems, this series was a disappointment. <br /><br />It has her usual themes from the Vorkosigan series: culture clash, younger woman/older man relationship, women's roles in a patriarchal society, and so forth. However, these themes are more clumsily executed. <br /><br />The culture clash theme is portrayed in the conflict between the settled farmers who want land to work while the Lakewalkers patrol these lands for evil magical disturbances and would rather the farmers stay in one place so as not to be a ready food source for those magical entities. <br /><br />Actually, the way the magical entities are described is pretty interesting, hinting at an ancient society of powerful sorcery gone wrong. However, Bujold brushes aside the epic story arc for a micro view. <br /><br />When Lakewalker Dag and Farmer Fawn get married, that is the minute examination of culture clash when each meets the other's families and tries to live in the other's fairly closed society, in a very similar way to Cordelia and Aral. But the ways in which the two cultures clash is fairly predictable and kind of meh.<br /><br />The culture clash idea is also a little irritating because it's obvious that the Lakewalkers are basically just white-washed Native American stereotypes. Even the landscape is pretty obviously North America (they boat down the Mississippi at one point) which makes the whole white-ified thing more annoying.<br /><br />Though one small aspect I did like was the contrast between the Northern Lakewalkers and the Southern Lakewalkers, demonstrating that the society is not one strict homogeneous culture. Still, that's not enough to save the whole book.<br /><br />Bujold as usual makes one society more feminist than the other, the Lakewalker society being matrilineal while the farmer society is both patrilineal and patriarchal. Fawn and Dag's sex life is very sex-positive in that they both enjoy it and take time with it. It is contrasted to the sex that Fawn had back on the farm which involved the double standards of a patriarchal society. Also, warning for her near rape in the beginning of the first book (which also is something that happens to Cordelia) as sexual violence against women in times of war is another theme of Bujold's. The whole sex positive part is done pretty well.<br /><br />I was disturbed by the 18 year old Fawn/55 year old Dag's relationship. When we read Fawn and Dag's feelings, we know that it's a pretty equal relationship, but personally, I still am disturbed. Especially when they first met because Dag saved Fawn from a near rape and subsequent miscarriage and then they get married after two weeks after which neither of them can really divorce each other without totally screwing themselves over.<br /><br />Also, Bujold has a theme of injured men and nursing women. That's pretty much the whole series. Dag has already lost a hand anyway, and then he spends like two books with a useless arm while Fawn nurses him through. Though that was a good theme in the beginning of Cordelia and Aral's relationship, and pretty great in Curse of Chalion with Cazaril (I felt it enhanced his religious blooming), it got a little tiresome in the Sharing Knife series.<br /><br />Bujold is careful to describe Dag's respect for Fawn's abilities, but it almost comes off as just too...fawning. (pun intended :P) Though both Fawn and Dag's abilities develop throughout the books, their relationship is just too saccharine. <br /><br />Basically I just thought Fawn and Dag were a little shallow compared to former characters, and that their relationship was too much Dag-as-a-teacher/explainer/awesome-sorcerer and Fawn-as-Dag's-loyal-supporter/military-backup. Though the world is well formed and the magic aspect nicely described, the characters just don't carry it out to the full potential. And the whole microview of a potential epic is also dissatisfying. All in all, a substandard story coming from a great author like Bujold. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12014166892405289115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_648148372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648148372" />
    <a title="Eliza Baum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5834453-eliza-baum"><img alt="Eliza Baum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597554577p2/5834453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648148372?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eliza Baum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eliza Baum" href="/user/show/5834453-eliza-baum">Eliza Baum</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer12212200773169997865">Second read 5/20/16:<br/><br/>I'm so sad that I'm done with this series again. The audio versions were fabulous, and it only added to how much I enjoy these characters. It had been just long enough since I read it that I had mostly forgotten the plot, but still remembered the <i>feel</i> of it. I will definitely be reading these again in a couple of years.<br/><br/>First read 6/22/13:<br/><br/>This was an enjoyable conclusion to the series.   <span id="freeText12212200773169997865" style="display:none">Second read 5/20/16:<br /><br />I'm so sad that I'm done with this series again. The audio versions were fabulous, and it only added to how much I enjoy these characters. It had been just long enough since I read it that I had mostly forgotten the plot, but still remembered the <i>feel</i> of it. I will definitely be reading these again in a couple of years.<br /><br />First read 6/22/13:<br /><br />This was an enjoyable conclusion to the series. Like the rest, it was really part of one long story, rather than being its own book. It added some more interesting characters--enough that, at one point, there were a good twenty secondary characters floating around. Many of the old favorites were there, too, which was nice. Despite his shaky beginnings, I really came to like Whit, and naturally Berry remained a favorite, too. Even Barr grew on me, which I completely didn't expect.<br /><br />I like how you can feel the progress in these books. The characters are constantly learning things, testing and changing their perception of the world, making mistakes and then correcting for them. Or not correcting for mistakes, and thus making for some nice antagonistic characters to balance things out.<br /><br />I recommend this series, but I definitely recommend reading all four in close succession. I think they would have lost something if I spaced them out more.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16580375642996662756">Oh, it was going so well!<br/><br/>Until near the end. <br/><br/>Fawn got SO short-changed. She flippin' changes a sharing knife into a sharing crossbow bolt on the battle field in the dark against a FLIPPIN' FLYING MALICE, and what does the narrative leave us with? Her being buried alive out of some Lakewalker patroller's ugly, ugly jealousy, and Dag's suffering at almost losing her.   <span id="freeText16580375642996662756" style="display:none">Oh, it was going so well!<br /><br />Until near the end. <br /><br />Fawn got SO short-changed. She flippin' changes a sharing knife into a sharing crossbow bolt on the battle field in the dark against a FLIPPIN' FLYING MALICE, and what does the narrative leave us with? Her being buried alive out of some Lakewalker patroller's ugly, ugly jealousy, and Dag's suffering at almost losing her. WHY IS NO ONE ASKING HER ABOUT HOW SHE REMADE THE WEAPON like they're asking Dag and Arkady about the ground shields?? Why is the story ignoring the really important part that Fawn played???<br /><br />From being a fleshed-out, gutsy, smart, and highly capable character, Fawn got demoted to a one-dimensional figurine whose main purpose seems to be keeping Dag sane and in love with the world. Dag got demoted, too, from a visionary to a broken man just hanging on by a little spark. Damn it, both of them are so much more than that!<br /><br />I thought this book was going in a different direction than it finally settled on, and the narrative peeled readers out of the multiple layers and dimensions of the main characters and their relationship as the story went on, until we were only left with shallow surface images at the end, a tableau that made me relieved, not sad, that the stories were ending.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7747721576430574154">The final volume in the Sharing Knife quartet. This is not a bad book, but I did find it to be rather a let down, especially after the previous volume, which was possibly my favorite of the series and seemed to be taking the whole thing in a new, bold, darker direction. Yet in this one, the worries that Dag might be tapping into something dark and dangerous with his powers are quickly shrugged off, and all the cool hints about the fallen civilization that the current Lakewalker/Farmer communitie</span>
  <span id="freeText7747721576430574154" style="display:none">The final volume in the Sharing Knife quartet. This is not a bad book, but I did find it to be rather a let down, especially after the previous volume, which was possibly my favorite of the series and seemed to be taking the whole thing in a new, bold, darker direction. Yet in this one, the worries that Dag might be tapping into something dark and dangerous with his powers are quickly shrugged off, and all the cool hints about the fallen civilization that the current Lakewalker/Farmer communities have replaced are seemingly forgotten. There’s one cool battle, but in general not much actually happens. Talk about going out with a whimper instead of a bang!<br /><br />Bujold is a good writer, and I pretty much enjoyed this book while I was reading it, but the more I think of it, the most frustrated I am by this as the conclusion to the series and by what that says about the priorities of the series in general.</span>

<div id="review_2727457393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2727457393" />
    <a title="Kathy Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3122948-kathy-martin"><img alt="Kathy Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459738550p2/3122948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2727457393?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Martin" href="/user/show/3122948-kathy-martin">Kathy Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2727457393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2685524013810185915">Now at the southern end of their journey, Dag has finally found a teacher who can help him learn more about his strange new powers. Arkady is a groundsetter and he recognizes that Dag, even though he is little trained, can be one too. The problem is find a place for Fawn in the Lakewalker camp where she is seen only as a farmer girl. Dag learns a lot in two months but he doesn't agree with the camp's policy of not providing healing for farmers. <br/><br/>When Finch, a young man Fawn has met at the camp ma</span>
  <span id="freeText2685524013810185915" style="display:none">Now at the southern end of their journey, Dag has finally found a teacher who can help him learn more about his strange new powers. Arkady is a groundsetter and he recognizes that Dag, even though he is little trained, can be one too. The problem is find a place for Fawn in the Lakewalker camp where she is seen only as a farmer girl. Dag learns a lot in two months but he doesn't agree with the camp's policy of not providing healing for farmers. <br /><br />When Finch, a young man Fawn has met at the camp market, comes and begs for assistance for his 5-year-old nephew who has lockjaw, Dag doesn't think twice before going to help even though it will likely cost him his place in the camp and his teacher. <br /><br />When he is kicked out of the camp, he and Fawn decide to work their way north again. She's newly pregnant and would like to find a home before her baby is born. At first, they decide to join a party which includes Finch and some of his friends but the party soon grows with the addition of Arkady and Barr. Also in the party are a couple of untrained half-breeds. They also meet again with Fawn's brother Whit, his wife Berry, and Berry's uncle and younger brother. <br /><br />Trailing both Dag and Arkady is a jealous young female patroller who has been trying to pry Dag loose from Fawn ever since she met him. Once she realizes that he is the hero of Wolf Ridge, she becomes even more determined to have him for her own. Dag isn't at all interested and is completely in love with and loyal to Fawn but Neeta isn't easily discouraged and reappears throughout the story trying one approach after another to separate Dag and Fawn.<br /><br />The trip is hard and made even harder when the group runs into two different malices. Luckily, Dag has been working on a way to protect Fawn and has expanded the protection to Fawn's brother Whit and his wife Berry. When the party is scattered during the malice attack, it is up to those protected farmers to find a way to save the group and introduce the malice to mortality. <br /><br />This was a wonderful story filled with great characters set in a well-developed world. It was about making small changes to bring about a changed future. Dag wants to change the dynamic between farmers and lakewalkers. He wants to change the world and pave the way for a future after the last malice has been destroyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2685524013810185915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2786818468" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2786818468" />
    <a title="Mikhail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25772487-mikhail"><img alt="Mikhail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455476005p2/25772487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2786818468?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikhail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikhail" href="/user/show/25772487-mikhail">Mikhail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2786818468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer461943572878188277">The Sharing Knife tetralogy is one any author would be proud to have. The characters are charming, the writing is a thing of beauty, and the world is profoundly fascinating, a kind of fantasy version of the American midwest with mild post-apocalyptic elements. I particularly enjoyed the loving accounts of flatboat sailing and trail riding in the second two books.<br/><br/>And yet... it's not quite Bujold's best work. I'd say the issue is two-fold. One, while the characters are generally very fun to read a</span>
  <span id="freeText461943572878188277" style="display:none">The Sharing Knife tetralogy is one any author would be proud to have. The characters are charming, the writing is a thing of beauty, and the world is profoundly fascinating, a kind of fantasy version of the American midwest with mild post-apocalyptic elements. I particularly enjoyed the loving accounts of flatboat sailing and trail riding in the second two books.<br /><br />And yet... it's not quite Bujold's best work. I'd say the issue is two-fold. One, while the characters are generally very fun to read about, they don't <i>quite</i> have the spark that you see in the Vorkosigan or Five Gods books. Dag is a good character, but Cazaril and Miles are absolutely masterful ones.<br /><br />The other issue is that the books feel almost... <i>small</i>... in comparison to Bujold's other work? Fundamentally, most of each book is a kind of Alternate 19th Century Slice of Live/Romance/Historical Fiction, and that <i>works</i>. But the Malices which are the great supernatural threat never seem to quite deliver after that first one. They're imposing and terrifying and yet they seem to go down very quickly, and the fascinating backstory about the Lake Lords and the shattered king is mostly an aside in the second book. The result is that while the Malices inform so much of the story, the story generally seems to work best without them -- the third book, which had purely human antagonists, also had the strongest conflict, I think.<br /><br />Anyway, I wouldn't make too much of this. These are still excellent books, and I read them quickly and with great enjoyment. I probably wouldn't make these the <i>first</i> Bujold books you read, but if you've read the <i>Curse of Chalion</i> or <i>The Vor Game</i> and liked them, definitely pick up the Sharing Knife books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="461943572878188277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  <span id="freeText3369097945737854738" style="display:none">The finale of the series, part two of book two. <br /><br />This felt like a very gentle closure of the series. <div id="review_1773413237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773413237" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4822789-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539442596p2/4822789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773413237?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/4822789-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4822789-christina?shelf=public-library">public-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4822789-christina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4822789-christina?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773413237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13584876505079197870">The final volume in this four-book fantasy series with a romance hook. There were many times I considered giving up on this book, because nothing happens for about 3/4 of the story. The central couple, who married at the end of book 1, adore and perfectly understand one another and there is never any conflict between them. An endless parade of secondary characters are introduced to the point it's hard to keep them all straight. <br/>It wasn't until I was about halfway through that I finally put my fi</span>
  <span id="freeText13584876505079197870" style="display:none">The final volume in this four-book fantasy series with a romance hook. There were many times I considered giving up on this book, because nothing happens for about 3/4 of the story. The central couple, who married at the end of book 1, adore and perfectly understand one another and there is never any conflict between them. An endless parade of secondary characters are introduced to the point it's hard to keep them all straight. <br />It wasn't until I was about halfway through that I finally put my finger on the problem with not just this book, but the series--the conflict is not in the central characters' power to resolve. Because the conflict is the prejudice that defines their world. He's a Lakewalker, a people with special powers who are the only ones who can defeat the evil Malices that spring up at random and can brainwash the weak minded Farmers. She's a Farmer, and ignorant nonmagical Farmers fear Lakewalkers, believing they eat the dead among other dreaded customs. And so the two people keep well apart, until these two are thrown together, and in an unprecedented feat defeat a Malice together, fall in love, and marry. That's book 1 which worked well. But for the remaining three books, the conflict they face is no one will accept their marriage--and you can't change prejudice in a matter of weeks, which is the longest time they spend anywhere. So they just seem to meander around for most of the series until a villain conveniently pops up toward the end of the book, is summarily defeated, and they resume their plodding along.<br />And then there's the lack of character flaws in the main characters. Dag, the hero, seems to be limitless in his remarkable abilities. Not only is he a great and renowned warrior, it turns out he discovers an ability to be a healer, and a magic knife maker, three very distinct professions in their world. He also manages to revolutionize the science and customs of their world (as does his wife, Fawn). To a degree, this is basic commercial fiction hero fare, so I just went with it. But it's not all that engaging as most of the novel is spent focusing on Dag figuring out and developing his special powers, and Fawn being supportive and only occasionally fussing at him. Okay, I'll admit, I kind of liked their sweet relationship--but it wasn't very interesting. I also have to admit the conflict at the end of this novel was much bigger than anything earlier in the series, so it did have a bit of an epic final battle feel that was well set up, which is why I bumped it from 2 stars to 3. <br />There's also the fact that he's in his 60s (a fact we're constantly reminded of as he refers mentally to himself as Old Patroller at least once a chapter, which grew almost as tiring as the expletive "Absent gods" that appeared about twice a chapter) and she turns 19 during the series. The only other couple that falls for one another has a similar age gap dynamic. Which was odd. <br />Overall, I rather wish I'd skimmed through the middle of these books, as at about 400 pages each, the pay-off wasn't quite worth the reading investment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13584876505079197870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_290818997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290818997" />
    <a title="heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19026-heidi"><img alt="heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302740285p2/19026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290818997?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="heidi" href="/user/show/19026-heidi">heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290818997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8737124260485402789">First, let me say that I am a Bujold fangirl, but not an uncritical one. I like some of the things she's done much more than I like other things. That's ok. I don't demand that a writer cater to my needs universally, or be consistently excellent (although I'd like that, of course).<br/><br/>The first book in this series tore at my heart because of personal connection. The last one was... boring. I suspect that I would like this series a lot better if it were two books instead of four. I can't argue with t</span>
  <span id="freeText8737124260485402789" style="display:none">First, let me say that I am a Bujold fangirl, but not an uncritical one. I like some of the things she's done much more than I like other things. That's ok. I don't demand that a writer cater to my needs universally, or be consistently excellent (although I'd like that, of course).<br /><br />The first book in this series tore at my heart because of personal connection. The last one was... boring. I suspect that I would like this series a lot better if it were two books instead of four. I can't argue with the theme of two conflicting groups uniting to the benefit of both, but I didn't find the characters very compelling.<br /><br />In this book (but it's hard to talk about the books in the series individually), we see the plot threads all get neatly wrapped up. Happy endings and hope for everyone. Babies! Houses! Careers! I thought it was all very predictable, although I did kind of love the new healer character.<br /><br />Huh. I think typing that made me figure out why Dag does nothing for me. He is not drawn as very joyous. And you'd think that maybe Aral isn't joyous, either, but there are glimpses and flashes of both his past and present where you can see that he has rejoiced in the past. I don't get that from Dag, although I think I should. His memories of his first wife are all poisoned, and his love for Fawn is more like he finds her...entertaining? Sparkly? Something. I think I am deeply bothered by the inequitable nature of their relationship. I think we are supposed to see that her ground makes her special, but mostly I find her a little like Nynaeve: stubborn, practical, deeply grounded in holding house, and perhaps not really exceptional? I don't know. I feel like I know a lot of women who are stubborn and practical and devoted. Perhaps the point is that she is a hero like any of us could be, but then she has this "specialness" which comes from nowhere other than the innate her-ness of her. Don't we all have that?<br /><br />TLDR: I don't understand the fundamental romance or the characters therein, and therefore the other plot is what the book depends on for me, and it is not compelling or developed enough to carry four books on its own.<br /><br />Read if: You've read the others and you'd like a sense of completion, you like the art of compromise, BABIES!<br /><br />Skip if: You have stalled out anywhere in the series, you have squicks about miscarriage or infertility, you are just looking for more Miles</span>
  <a data-text-id="8737124260485402789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91936185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91936185" />
    <a title="Lighthearted" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1132923-lighthearted"><img alt="Lighthearted" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372874200p2/1132923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91936185?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lighthearted" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lighthearted" href="/user/show/1132923-lighthearted">Lighthearted</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91936185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer320157613668845034">Dag and Fawn continue their mission to bring Lakewalkers and farmers together. Dag also finds a Lakewalker Maker willing to train him. Predictably, Dag pushes the limits of his host Lakewalker camp and he and Fawn must travel onward in search of a home. Predictably, they also gather an assortment of characters to join their journey.<br/><br/>Dag and Fawn both annoy me a great deal in this installment. While I want their mission to succeed, I want it to seem less preachy and I want them to be less “perfect</span>
  <span id="freeText320157613668845034" style="display:none">Dag and Fawn continue their mission to bring Lakewalkers and farmers together. Dag also finds a Lakewalker Maker willing to train him. Predictably, Dag pushes the limits of his host Lakewalker camp and he and Fawn must travel onward in search of a home. Predictably, they also gather an assortment of characters to join their journey.<br /><br />Dag and Fawn both annoy me a great deal in this installment. While I want their mission to succeed, I want it to seem less preachy and I want them to be less “perfect”. Dag often expresses angst but it never feels true to me, particularly when he becomes more ambitious with his experiments. Although her intentions are admirable and she has likeable qualities, Fawn comes across as a preachy know-it-all—I want to like her but she annoys me to no end. I also want to see a real relationship between them—all that we see of Dag and Fawn is complete understanding all of the time—which is a nice concept but it does not feel real.<br /><br />In addition to my annoyance with Dag and Fawn, the first half of the book was agonizingly slow—I understand that trying to overcome decades of prejudice is a slow process but it was also predictable, preachy and boring. It also dominated the story, leaving other facets largely unexplored. There’s the issue of whether it’s ever okay to place a persuasion on someone (which goes along with the Lakewalkers’ ability to read farmers’ grounds and determine if they are lying). The “protection” Dag has been working on continues the storyline but it still receives less attention in the story than it warrants, particularly as this is supposed to be the last volume of the series. I also really wanted to see more progress in the understanding of what Malices are and what causes them to appear. Finally, Bujold piqued our curiosity about this world’s ancient history and “people across the sea” but as of yet hasn’t taken that storyline any further.<br /><br />I did enjoy the Arkady &amp; Sumac storyline, all descriptions of Copperhead, and the Malice scenes. Overall, I rate the book as okay. Even though this is supposed to be the concluding volume of the series, I hope that Bujold revisits the series because there’s a lot of story left to tell; I just hope that the pace is quickened and there’s a bit more drama.</span>
  <a data-text-id="320157613668845034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070275050?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/5229815-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229815-kate?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229815-kate?shelf=2014">2014</a>
